114 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Pope v. Easley


No. 206PA01


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 544; 556 S.E.2d 265; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1237


September 10, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
December 18, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of an order and judgment entered on 14 February 2001 by Farmer, J., in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee legislator filed a declaratory judgment action in the Superior Court of Wake County, North Carolina, against appellant state officials and judges challenging the constitutionality of an amendment to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-16 increasing the number of judges on the court of appeals. The trial court held a portion of the statute unconstitutional and severed that portion from the remainder of the statute. The officials and judges appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state general assembly passed an amendment to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-16 in 2000 which purported to increase the size of the state court of appeals from 12 to 15 judges. The statute provided that each of the new judgeships would be created at the time of appointment of an individual to the particular position and that each judge would thereafter hold office until facing an initial retention election in 2005. The legislator argued that the provision allowing the new judges to serve for that period of time conflicted with the provisions of N.C. Const. art. IV, § 19, which required a judge appointed to a vacancy to stand for election at the next general election. The appellate court held that the statute did in fact conflict with the state constitution and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 163-9 and was therefore unconstitutional. Despite the legislature's attempt to make the judgeships effective on appointment, the judgeships were created by the statute, and vacancies in those judgeships had to be filled according to law. The remaining portions of the statute could however stand alone and the trial court had properly given effect to a severance clause.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

115 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Westminster Homes, Inc. v. Town of Cary Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


No. 499PA00


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 298; 554 S.E.2d 634; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1089


May 15, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
November 9, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N. C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, Westminster Homes, Inc. v. Town of Cary Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 140 N.C. App. 99, 535 S.E.2d 415 (2000), reversing and remanding an order signed 24 March 1999 by Cashwell, J., in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner homeowners appealed the determination of respondent zoning board that they were in violation of a zoning ordinance. The trial court reversed the zoning board's decision, but the North Carolina Court of Appeals affirmed the board. The homeowners sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner developer proposed a subdivision opposed by neighboring residents. The parties negotiated a conditional use zoning permit providing a buffer between the developments including a fence. Some land which made up the buffer was included in the lots sold to the homeowners. As a result, the fence divided their property. They installed gates in the fence to allow access to their property on the opposite side of the fence and were notified this violated the conditional use permit. The permit conveyed a clear desire for privacy through a wide buffer including a fence restricting residential access, which was to be undisturbed, and did not provide for gates. The landowners argued they were liable for torts and taxes in connection with land to which they had no access, but there was no reasonable basis for tort liability absent willful action and the lack of access potentially reduced their tax liabilities. This was not an unconstitutional "taking" of the homeowners' private property as no new conditions on the homeowners' use were imposed and the permit was not imposed by a legislative or regulatory body, but was requested and negotiated by the developer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

116 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


No. 556A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 268; 553 S.E.2d 885; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1090


September 12, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
November 9, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Parker v. North Carolina, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4081 (U.S. June 3, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Smith (W. Osmond), J., on 1 April 1999 in Superior Court, Wake County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. On 5 January 2001, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to her appeal of an additional judgment.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The jury for the Superior Court, Wake County, North Carolina, found defendant guilty of first-degree kidnapping and of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation, and under the felony murder rule. The jury recommended a sentence of death for the first-degree murder conviction, and the trial court entered judgment in accordance with that recommendation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Viewed in the light most favorable to the State, the evidence was sufficient to permit a jury to find defendant killed the victim with premeditation and deliberation. In addition, the supreme court found that the kidnapping and felony murder convictions were supported by sufficient evidence. Also, a rational jury could have concluded defendant had no significant history of prior criminal activity. Accordingly, the trial court properly submitted the N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(f)(1) (1999) mitigating circumstance to the jury. However, the supreme court found no indication that the sentence of death was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Therefore, after concluding its proportionality review, based upon the characteristics of defendant and the crimes she committed, the supreme court was convinced that the sentence of death recommended by the jury and ordered by the trial court was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The supreme court determined that there was no error in the trial court's judgment and sentence.

 

117 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Piedmont Triad Airport Auth. v. Urbine


No. 367PA00


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 336; 554 S.E.2d 331; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1095


March 14, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
November 9, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied April 1, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2177.


PRIOR HISTORY: On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of an order entered on 20 April 2000 by DeRamus, J., in Superior Court, Guilford County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee airport authority filed an action in the Superior Court, Guilford County (North Carolina), to condemn appellant landowner's property. The trial court ruled in favor of the authority, and the landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under the authority's proposal, an air cargo company would construct a building on the condemned land, to expand its already existing facility, and pay rent to the airport authority. This action involved a reasonable connection with the convenience and necessity of the airport authority, which was publicly created, because it would locate an air cargo facility next to existing airport runways and facilities. The activity also had to benefit the public generally, as opposed to special interests or persons. The public expressed its desire in N.C. Const. art. V, § 13, to develop airports and seaports. This provision did not conflict with the requirement of N.C. Const. art. V, § 2(1), that taxation be exercised for a public purpose. The two provisions acted in concert so that any activity pursuant to art. V, § 13(1)(a), could be fully realized insofar as it was for a public purpose or public use. The public's desire to develop airports included the physical expansion of the air cargo company's facilities on the airport authority's property. Therefore, the envisioned use of the condemned property was constitutionally permissible.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

118 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Fennell v. Stephenson


No. 267PA00


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 327; 554 S.E.2d 629; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1096


March 12, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
November 9, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 137 N.C. App. 430, 528 S.E.2d 911 (2000), affirming in part and reversing in part an order entered by Eagles, J., on 15 February 1999 in Superior Court, Guilford County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; discretionary review improvidently allowed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following affirmance of the dismissal of its federal claims, plaintiff estate filed suit in the state court against defendants, patrolman and state highway patrol. The trial court granted the defendants' motion to dismiss. The North Carolina Court of Appeals reversed, in part, allowing the estate's unconstitutional detention and equal protection claims to proceed. The patrolman and state highway patrol appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claim was premised on events that occurred when the patrolman stopped and killed the decedent. That was when the statutes of limitation began to run. On appeal, the patrolman and the state highway patrol argued that the statute of limitations had run on the estate's claims. The supreme court agreed and held that if the estate sought recovery for state constitutional violations, it should have named the patrolman in his official capacity. The estate failed to name the patrolman in his official capacity until almost five years after the cause of action accrued, and almost two years after the statute of limitations had expired. Thus, the claim for unreasonable detention against the patrolman was barred by the statute of limitations. As to the state highway patrol, the estate failed to name it as a party until the amended complaint more than five years after the decedent was stopped and killed and more than two years after the statute of limitations expired. The addition of the highway patrol in the amended state complaint did not relate back to the original state complaint because the relation back doctrine did not apply to parties, only to claims.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the court of appeals on the two issues presented, thereby reinstating the trial court's order dismissing all claims against the state patrolman and the state highway patrol. The supreme court also held that it improvidently allowed discretionary review on any additional issues not specifically addressed in this opinion.

State v. Ward

Stay granted by State v. Ward, 676 S.E.2d 898, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 559 (N.C., 2009)
Motion dismissed by State v. Ward, 684 S.E.2d 40, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 726 (N.C., 2009)
Writ granted by State v. Ward, 363 N.C. 588, 684 S.E.2d 39, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 813 (2009)
Motion granted by State v. Ward, 684 S.E.2d 688, 2009 N.C. LEXIS 888 (N.C., 2009)
Motion dismissed by, As moot State v. Ward, 2010 N.C. LEXIS 489 (N.C., June 16, 2010)
Later proceeding at State v. Ward, 2010 N.C. LEXIS 418 (N.C., June 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Sumner, J., on 15 December 1998 in Superior Court, Halifax County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. On 30 March 2000, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.
State v. Ward, 543 S.E.2d 156, 2000 N.C. LEXIS 252 (N.C., 2000)



DISPOSITION: No error in guilt phase, death sentence vacated, and remanded for new capital sentencing proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Halifax County (North Carolina), upon a jury verdict, found defendant guilty of, among other things, first-degree felony murder. In a separate capital sentencing proceeding, one mitigating and three aggravating circumstances were found and he was sentenced to, among other things, death. The North Carolina Supreme Court allowed his motion to bypass the court of appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.


OVERVIEW: Codefendants with plea arrangements testified that defendant was told of a plan to steal from a residence, was interested, and recruited one of them. The three, with another, went to the house, but felt thwarted by the resident's presence. The recruit suggested they break in and subdue her. The original planner was concerned about being identified. Defendant suggested that a dead person could not talk. The recruit said he would kill her, and with defendant burst in and beat her. Defendant shot her twice and was arrested after he and his recruit tried to withdraw money from her account. The supreme court held that the prosecutor, in sentencing arguments, impermissibly commented on defendant's invocation of his right to silence, and the trial court wrongly failed to intervene ex mero motu. As voir dire was conducted individually, the prosecutor's remarks to 16 veniremembers about defendant's right to testify did not constitute improper "extended comment." Although veniremembers were unable to articulate their bias against capital punishment clearly, they were properly challenged for cause because their answers contained strong reservations about capital punishment.


OUTCOME: The conviction of first-degree murder was upheld. The death sentence was set aside and the case was remanded for a new capital sentencing proceeding on the first-degree murder conviction.

State v. Taylor


No. 505A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 28; 550 S.E.2d 141; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 832


February 12, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]

Writ of habeas corpus denied Taylor v. State, 356 N.C. 695, 577 S.E.2d 108, 2003 N.C. LEXIS 140 (2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Taylor, 2007 N.C. LEXIS 1238 (N.C., Dec. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Fullwood, J., on 23 October 1998 in Superior Court, New Hanover County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. On 24 February 2000, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of an additional judgment.
State v. Taylor, 542 S.E.2d 664, 2000 N.C. LEXIS 209 (N.C., 2000)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the New Hanover County Superior Court (North Carolina) of first-degree murder and armed robbery with a dangerous weapon. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murder and 103 to 133 months imprisonment for the robbery. Defendant appealed the murder conviction to the North Carolina Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed the victim because he was upset by conflicting stories of what had happened to drugs and money in the victim's possession. An arrest warrant was issued for defendant and he was detained in Florida pending extradition to North Carolina. North Carolina detectives went to Florida and obtained a confession from defendant. On appeal, the supreme court found (1) the trial court did not err in denying defendant a continuance since defense counsel had adequate notice that the trial was imminent and had a reasonable time to prepare for trial; (2) defendant's right to counsel did not attach prior to or during his confinement for extradition to North Carolina and his confession was properly admitted at trial; (3) the trial court did not err in questioning permitted of prospective jurors or in striking a juror for cause; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that a witness was not qualified to testify as to the position of the victim's body when he was shot; (5) the trial court's final list of mitigating circumstances subsumed the proposed mitigating circumstances to the exclusion of none; and (6) the sentence of death was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

State v. Bone


No. 281A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


354 N.C. 1; 550 S.E.2d 482; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 833


March 14, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
August 17, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 18, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1737.
Writ of certiorari denied Bone v. North Carolina, 535 U.S. 940, 122 S. Ct. 1323, 152 L. Ed. 2d 231, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1737 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability granted Bone v. Polk, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69233 (M.D.N.C., July 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Steelman, J., on 5 February 1999 in Superior Court, Guilford County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.
State v. Bone, 547 S.E.2d 46, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 206 (N.C., 2001)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court, Guilford County (North Carolina), of first-degree murder and two counts of burglary. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murder conviction and consecutive prison sentences of 146 to 185 months for the burglary convictions. Defendant appealed the murder conviction and sentence to the North Carolina Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant left a shoe print behind when he robbed and murdered a woman at her home. A detective was able to identify the shoe which left the print. An anonymous tip informed the detective that defendant was the murderer. The detective found defendant wearing the type of shoes that left a print and asked defendant to go to the police station. When defendant refused to allow the detective to examine his shoes, the detective left defendant waiting in an interrogation room with the door closed and an officer outside while he obtained a search warrant. When the detective returned, he seized defendant's shoes and left him in the same room with the door closed and the officer outside. After examining the shoes, the detective arrested defendant. Defendant then confessed to the murder. On appeal, the supreme court found the detective properly seized the shoes pursuant to the plain view doctrine and subject to a search incident to a lawful arrest because defendant was placed under "arrest" at the moment his shoes were seized. Further, defendant's arrest was supported by probable cause. Therefore, defendant's confession was not obtained through an illegal seizure or arrest.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lucas


No. 278PA00


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 568; 548 S.E.2d 712; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 668


February 14, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
July 20, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 138 N.C. App. 226, 530 S.E.2d 602 (2000), finding error in judgments entered 24 February 1998 by Bowen, J., in Superior Court, Harnett County, and ordering a new trial. On 12 July 2000, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's conditional petition for discretionary review as to additional issues. On 5 October 2000, the Supreme Court agreed to hear defendant's motion for appropriate relief and ordered both parties to file supplemental briefs.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; NO ERROR IN PART; SENTENCES VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED FOR NEW SENTENCING HEARING IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree burglary and second-degree kidnapping as an aider and abettor for both, and possession of a weapon of mass destruction; acquitted of first-degree murder and conspiracy charges; and sentenced to consecutive terms of imprisonment of 124 to 146, 85 to 99, and 16 to 20 months respectively. The North Carolina Court of Appeals ordered a new trial. The State's and defendant's petitions for review were allowed.


OVERVIEW: Given the rule that unless favorable to the State, defendant's evidence was not to be considered on sufficiency review, the record showed that defendant: spent the day with his friend, armed himself when he saw his friend arm himself, clad only in black accompanied his friend that night to a home, stood by holding his shotgun while his friend argued with the friend's ex-girlfriend and pointed his pistol at her, followed his friend into the home and stood inside armed while his friend shot a man numerous times, drove his friend and the abducted woman away remarking that his friend should have killed her too, hid the murder weapon, and returned to his friend's hotel room with clothes for the woman whom his friend raped. The North Carolina Supreme Court held that this showed that defendant had the requisite criminal intent to aid his friend. Because his indictment did not charge the statutory factors for an enhancement, nor were they submitted to the jury, the trial court improperly imposed a N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1340.16A enhanced sentence in violation of Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals was reversed as to the issue raised by the State. The trial court properly instructed as to defendant's specific intent to commit kidnapping and burglary. The sentences for those offenses were vacated and the matter remanded. Defendant was granted a new sentencing hearing as to the firearm enhancement. As to defendant's additional issues for discretionary review, there was no error.

State v. Jaynes


No. 194A92-2


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 534; 549 S.E.2d 179; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 672

July 20, 2001, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a 4 June 1999 judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Johnston, J., at a resentencing proceeding held in Superior Court, Polk County, upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder on the basis of malice, premeditation, and deliberation and of felony murder, and of other charges. On appeal, judgment on his larceny convictions was arrested and a new capital sentencing proceeding granted. The Superior Court, Polk County (North Carolina) jury found two N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(e)(5) aggravators, again recommended death, and defendant was so sentenced. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Several witnesses testified of defendant's plan to kill a rich man for money, and of defendant's admissions. Defendant admitted to telling his codefendant to lie and testified that he was remorseful and had not intended the killing. The jury found that the murder was committed while defendant was engaged in first-degree burglary and armed robbery. Upon resentencing he was sentenced to death. The State could suggest prison life was not harsh enough, and tell the jury not to be numb to this crime's violence.


OUTCOME: No error was found.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Morgan (Melzer A., Jr.), J., on 23 November 1998 in Superior Court, Guilford County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Guilford County (North Carolina), jury convicted defendant of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation; found one aggravating and one mitigating circumstance: N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 15A-2000(e)(3) and 15A-2000(f)(2) respectively; and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder in 1967 for the murder of his first wife. In 1988, defendant shot and killed his second wife, for which he was convicted and sentenced nine years later. The North Carolina Supreme Court held that defendant waived his right to a competency hearing by not asserting it. Evidence of past treatment alone was not substantial evidence that he was incompetent. State explanations for peremptory challenges were race-neutral. The victim's diary was admissible under the state-of-mind hearsay exception. Five days notice from the State to defendant, of its intent to introduce statements of four witnesses who had died, was adequate. The statements were reliable and probative. Defendant's argument that based on his desire to reconcile with the victim, it was possible that a conflict erupted between the two, was not sufficient to negate premeditation and deliberation evidence and warrant a second-degree murder instruction. Evidence including photos relating to the prior murder was properly admissible at sentencing. The jury was properly instructed as to unanimity. The sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: No error was found in the superior court's judgment.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a 21 May 1999 judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Doughton, J., at a resentencing proceeding held in Superior Court, Wilkes County, upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder.

DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Wilkes County, North Carolina, convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. The defendant appealed his sentence of death to the North Carolina Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered the victim. The appellate court found that (1) the voir dire was proper; (2) the trial court properly instructed the jury; (3) the trial court did not infringe upon defendant's statutory right to assistance of two attorneys in a capital trial; (4) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to continue; and (5) the prosecutor's jury argument was not improper. While the jury found five statutory mitigating circumstances, it also found four aggravating circumstances, three of which standing alone would be sufficient to support a sentence of death. Therefore, the appellate court determined that the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant received a fair capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error. Therefore, the sentence of death recommended by the jury and entered by the trial court was left undisturbed.

State v. Mitchell


No. 217A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 309; 543 S.E.2d 830; 2001 N.C. LEXIS 265


February 14, 2001, Heard In the Supreme Court  
April 6, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10083.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of death entered by Allen (J.B., Jr.), J., on 4 November 1997 in Superior Court, Wake County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of three counts of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for three counts of first-degree murder, and was tried capitally, in the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), and found guilty on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and under the felony murder rule. The jury recommended a sentence of death for each conviction and the trial court entered judgment accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed two victims after searching a victim's home for weapons, and an accomplice killed a third victim. After defendant's arrest, he was given Miranda warnings, and confessed to an unrelated burglary three hours later. He was given lunch, and, six and one-half hours after the Miranda warnings, confessed to the murders. The Miranda warnings were not stale at the time of the murder confession. The short-form indictment used, and authorized by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15-144, was constitutional. During voir dire, defendant could not properly ask prospective jurors their verdict under a given set of facts, or inquire into all aspects of their private lives or religious beliefs. When defense counsel and defendant reached an impasse over rehabilitating a panel member who said she would base her decision on emotional sympathy for the victims, defendant's decision controlled. Trial court's failure to intervene ex mero motu in prosecutor's argument was not error, and, when prosecutor commented defendant had a right to testify, it was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. After comparing defendant's case to other capital cases, his death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed because his confession was properly admitted, his indictment form was constitutional, voir dire was not improperly limited, prosecutorial mention of his right to testify and the trial court's failure to intervene ex mero motu was harmless error, and his sentence was proportional.

State v. Holman


No. 200A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 174; 540 S.E.2d 18; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 909


October 16, 2000, Heard In the Supreme Court  
December 21, 2000, Filed Certiorari Denied ;October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6866.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Holman, 353 N.C. 389, 547 S.E.2d 29, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 13 (2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Holman v. North Carolina, 534 U.S. 910, 151 L. Ed. 2d 181, 122 S. Ct. 250, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6866 (2001)
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Holman, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 847 (N.C., Aug. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Spencer (James C., Jr.), J., on 7 April 1998 in Superior Court, Wake County, upon defendant's plea of guilty of first-degree murder.
State v. Holman, 544 S.E.2d 567, 2000 N.C. LEXIS 605 (N.C., 2000)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), upon defendant's plea of guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: After threatening and stalking his estranged wife, defendant gunned her down in a parking lot. Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder after the issuance of a short-form indictment. A jury recommended the death sentence. The court held that the indictment did not violate defendant's constitutional rights because defendant had notice that he was charged with first-degree murder and the elements thereof, and that he could be subjected to the death penalty, and the State was not required to allege the aggravating circumstances. There was sufficient evidence of aggravating circumstances because defendant's actions were calculated to torture the victim psychologically and to leave her aware that she was helpless to prevent impending death, and the method chosen by defendant to carry out the killing was conscienceless and pitiless, inflicting excessive fear and psychological torture. The trial court did not err in deferring its ruling on whether introduction of certain evidence by defendant would permit the State to introduce irrelevant and prejudicial evidence because defendant's decision not to introduce the evidence was purely tactical and did not implicate any of his rights.


OUTCOME: There was no error in the judgment imposing the death sentence because the short-form indictment for first-degree murder provided notice of the charge, the elements thereof, and the possibility of the death penalty; defendant's intention to psychologically torture victim was sufficient evidence of an aggravating circumstance; and defendant's decision not to introduce certain evidence was tactical and did not implicate any of his rights.

State v. Grooms


No. 39A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 50; 540 S.E.2d 713; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 895


September 11, 2000, Heard In the Supreme Court  
December 21, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5838.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Ellis (B. Craig), J., on 24 April 1998 in Superior Court, Scotland County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. On 26 October 1999, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Scotland County (North Carolina) finding him guilty of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation, deliberation, and under the felony murder rule, and sentencing him to death for the victim's murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was denied his constitutional right to a speedy trial. The record showed that much of the delay was attributable to defendant's unwillingness to cooperate with his attorneys; thus, he could not complain about the delay and his constitutional right to a speedy trial was not denied. Defendant also contended that he was deprived of his constitutional right to effective assistance of counsel. The court found that there was no reasonable probability that any of the alleged errors of defense counsel affected the outcome of the trial. Thus, defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was denied. Defendant's pretrial motion to suppress and motion in limine were not sufficient to preserve questions for the appeal. In the absence of any evidence suggesting that defendant was incompetent, the trial court did not err in deciding not to order the mental health evaluation. The jury found five aggravating circumstances were present in victim's murder and the court found that the death penalty was given in similar cases; thus, the sentence of death was proportionate and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error; defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error, and that the death sentence was not disproportionate. Accordingly, the judgments of the trial court were left undisturbed.

 

129 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. North Carolina Dep't of Revenue


No. 56PA00-2


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 142; 540 S.E.2d 313; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 896


October 18, 2000, Heard In the Supreme Court  
December 21, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N. C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of an order entered on 24 March 2000 by Thompson, J., in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general challenged the order of the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina) granting attorney's fees to prevailing plaintiffs in a class action against the State. The court granted plaintiff's discretionary review motion.


OVERVIEW: The matter was before the court on appeal from the trial court's order granting attorney's fees to counsel representing prevailing plaintiffs in a class action against the State. Appellant, as attorney general for the State, challenged the fees awarded to opposing counsel and whether such fees were excessive. The case commenced nearly a decade before as a certified class action involving approximately 200,000 class members who alleged that a tax imposed on their retirement benefits was illegal. The State agreed to a settlement which provided an award of attorney's fees to class counsel of $ 63,920,000. The agreement signed by the State also contained a waiver clause which stated attorney's fees would be determined by the court and the State, as represented by the attorney general, waiving any rights to be heard concerning these matters. The court found this language to bar appellant from any claim to the attorney's fee award, and despite his common law powers, he had no power to act to defend the people's interest. The court further found appellant had no power to intervene under N.C. R. Civ. P. 24.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed. Appellant lacked standing to challenge the fees awarded, based upon his waiver to contest the award signed as part of the settlement agreement. His service as state counsel did not grant him extraordinary power to take actions necessary for the protection of the public interest.

State v. Davis


No. 109A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


353 N.C. 1; 539 S.E.2d 243; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 897


May 16, 2000, Heard In the Supreme Court  
December 21, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5852.
Writ of certiorari denied Davis v. North Carolina, 534 U.S. 839, 122 S. Ct. 95, 151 L. Ed. 2d 55, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5852 (2001)
Related proceeding at State v. Davis, 359 N.C. 71, 604 S.E.2d 919, 2004 N.C. LEXIS 1437 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Davis v. Polk, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 72978 (W.D.N.C., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Payne Ronald K., J., on 21 August 1997 in Superior Court, Buncombe County, following a plea of guilty of first-degree murder. On 24 September 1999, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of an additional judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment without parole following a second plea of guilty of first-degree murder.
State v. Davis, 540 S.E.2d 35, 1999 N.C. LEXIS 1133 (N.C., 1999)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina), which entered a judgment imposing a sentence of death, following defendant's plea of guilty to first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to the first-degree murders of his aunt and cousin. The jury found aggravating circumstances and recommended a sentence of death for the murder of appellant's aunt. On appeal, defendant challenged the death sentence, arguing, inter alia, that the trial court violated state and federal constitutional law during sentencing deliberations by responding improperly to the jury's question about the result of an inability to agree, and a juror's letter indicating an inability to continue as a member of the jury. The court affirmed. Defendant was present when the proceeding in question took place. The trial court heard from counsel and responded in open court to each of the communications. The fair and accurate disclosure of the substantive content of the communications was sufficient to render counsel the full opportunity to effectively represent defendant. As such, defense counsel had the opportunity to object to the proposed instruction. Therefore there was no violation of defendant's rights. The court concluded that defendant's capital sentencing proceeding was free of prejudicial error and that the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The trial court did not violate the defendant's right by refusing to disclose the full content of notes from the jury to the trial judge. The fair and accurate disclosure of the substantive content of the notes was sufficient to render counsel the full opportunity to effectively represent defendant. Defendant was present when the proceeding took place, and counsel responded in open court to each of the communications.

State v. Cummings


No. 65A87-3


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


352 N.C. 600; 536 S.E.2d 36; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 753


September 20, 1999, Heard In the Supreme Court  
October 6, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 23, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3277.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Ellis, J., on 11 November 1997 after a capital resentencing proceeding held in Superior Court, Robeson County.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), alleging numerous constitutional and procedural errors, from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by the Robeson County Superior Court (North Carolina), after a jury again found aggravating circumstances outweighing mitigating circumstances after defendant's conviction of murder.


OVERVIEW: In 1987, defendant was convicted of first degree murder and he was sentenced to death. Three years later, upon the United States Supreme Court's remand of the case, the court vacated defendant's sentence of death and remanded for a new capital sentencing proceeding. The sentencing jury again recommended a sentence of death. Defendant appealed as of right. Concluding that defendant's capital resentencing proceeding was free of prejudicial error and that the death sentence was not disproportionate under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(d)(20) (1999), the court upheld defendant's sentence of death. The court specifically held that the State did not engage in prosecutorial misconduct in conducting discovery and defendant had no right to be present during the preliminary qualification of prospective jurors. Further, although defendant could not have received the death penalty for his 1966 plea of guilty to murder, such crime was still a "capital felony" for purposes of the aggravator, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(e)(2) (1999).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; although defendant pled guilty to murder and, under the now repealed statute, his case was not a "capital case," the crime was still a "capital felony" for purposes of the aggravating circumstance. Furthermore, nothing in the record suggested that the death sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor or was other disproportionate.

State v. Brewington


No. 252A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


352 N.C. 489; 532 S.E.2d 496; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 616


May 15, 2000, Heard in the Supreme Court  
August 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 20, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1416.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of death entered by Bowen, J., on 28 August 1998 in Superior Court, Harnett County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. On 26 October 1999, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment of the Harnett County Superior Court, North Carolina, convicting him of two counts of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by jury of first-degree arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, two counts of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and under the felony murder rule. He was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), arguing first that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress statements made to officers. Specifically, defendant argued the statements should have been excluded from evidence because they were made at a time when defendant was subjected to custodial interrogation and was not advised of his Miranda rights. The court disagreed, finding the statements were noncustodial and were made freely and voluntarily. Next, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for discovery and production of the documents relating to the polygraph examination taken. The court concluded that polygrams did not fall within the category of "physical or mental examinations" contemplated under of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-903. Finally, the court concluded that the trial court committed no error in refusing to submit defendant's proposed nonstatutory mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; court concluded that the defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding, free of prejudicial error. Moreover, the court could not conclude as a matter of law that the sentence of death was excessive or disproportionate.

State v. Smith


No. 279A99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


352 N.C. 531; 532 S.E.2d 773; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 617


May 17, 2000, Heard in the Supreme Court  
August 25, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Downs, J., on 23 April 1998 in Superior Court, Buncombe County, upon defendant's plea of guilty of first-degree murder and a jury's recommendation of a sentence of death. On 26 October 1999, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death upon defendant's plea of guilty to first-degree murder and the jury's recommendation of death. Defendant also appealed the lesser sentences imposed for his pleas of guilty to first-degree burglary, first-degree forcible rape, first-degree arson, and robbery with a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder, first-degree burglary, first-degree forcible rape, first-degree arson, and robbery with a dangerous weapon. Upon the jury's recommendation, the trial court imposed a sentence of death for the murder. Lesser sentences were imposed for each of the other felonies. Defendant appealed his sentences. The court found no error in the sentences for the following reasons. First, the indictments based on N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15-144 complied with both the North Carolina and the United States Constitutions. Second, plaintiff's articulated reasons for exercising its peremptory challenges did not appear to have been motivated by purposeful discrimination, but appeared both race-neutral and otherwise beyond reproach. Third, the trial court had no duty to expound on the direct consequences of defendant's guilty pleas beyond what was mandated by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1022(a) (1999), absent an indication by defendant that he required such instruction. Finally, the photographs of the victim, which were shown to the sentencing jury, were not so numerous or egregious as to render the sentencing hearing fundamentally unfair.


OUTCOME: No error was found in the sentences imposed by the trial court. One reason was that plaintiff's articulated reasons for exercising its peremptory challenges appeared both race-neutral and otherwise beyond reproach. Another reason was that the trial court had no duty to expound on the direct consequences of defendant's guilty pleas beyond what was statutorily mandated, absent an indication by defendant that he required such instruction.

State v. Steen


No. 530A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


352 N.C. 227; 536 S.E.2d 1; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 530


April 17, 2000, Heard In the Supreme Court  
July 13, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 20, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 1450.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Downs, J., on 28 August 1998 in Superior Court, Mecklenburg County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 31 August 1999.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment in the Superior Court, Mecklenburg County (North Carolina), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted defendant of first-degree murder, and imposed a sentence of death .


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested on drug charges, he was connected with an elderly woman's death and convicted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding: officers' observation defendant's erratic operation of his bicycle was sufficient to raise reasonable suspicion for investigatory stop; defendant voluntarily consented to search of his person; officers properly obtained defendant's bloody clothing; neither court order nor search warrant was necessary for police to take hair and saliva samples from defendant; arresting officer acted in good faith in informing magistrate of approximate date of murder; denial of defendant's motion to rehabilitate each juror challenged for cause was proper; evidence of defendant's immaturity was not so substantial as to require trial court to submit age mitigator ex mero motu; defendant's evidence as to mental disturbance was not uncontroverted, thus peremptory instruction was not required; trial court's error in stating that findings of mitigating circumstances were to be unanimous was merely lapsus linguae and harmless error; State's closing argument regarding grand jury's role in determining alleged date of offenses was proper response.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Officers had reasonable suspicion to conduct investigatory stop. Officers applying for search warrant acted in good faith, and there was sufficient showing of probable cause to justify search warrant. Court was not required to offer peremptory instruction on defendant's mental disturbance, as defendant's evidence was not uncontroverted. State's closing argument in determining alleged date of murder was proper.

State v. Hyde


No. 529A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


352 N.C. 37; 530 S.E.2d 281; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 443


March 14, 2000, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 16, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied January 16, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 738.
Writ of certiorari denied Hyde v. North Carolina, 531 U.S. 1114, 121 S. Ct. 862, 148 L. Ed. 2d 775, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 738 (2001)
Motion granted by State v. Hyde, 618 S.E.2d 234, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 731 (N.C., 2005)
Writ denied by State v. Hyde, 360 N.C. 72, 623 S.E.2d 779, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1126 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Wainwright, J., on 23 July 1998 in Superior Court, Onslow County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. On 21 April 1999, the Supreme Court allowed defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments.
State v. Hyde, 535 S.E.2d 44, 1999 N.C. LEXIS 304 (N.C., 1999)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Onslow County (North Carolina), imposing a sentence of death upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and under the felony-murder rule, first-degree burglary, and conspiracy to commit first-degree burglary, for killing a man in his home during an attempt to steal drugs. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murder. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court did not err in finding that defendant voluntarily confessed to police, or in denying defendant's motion for individual voir dire and sequestration of the jurors during voir dire. The trial court did not err in admitting photographs of the victim that depicted the large number of wounds and also corroborated defendant's confession. Submission of the aggravating circumstance that the murder was committed to avoid lawful arrest was proper because the evidence showed the victim was killed so he would not report the burglary. The death penalty was not disproportionate, given the finding of premeditation and deliberation and the fact that defendant killed the defenseless victim in his home.


OUTCOME: The judgment was left undisturbed because defendant's trial and capital sentencing proceeding were free from prejudicial error and the death penalty was not excessive or disproportionate.

 

141 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foreman


No. 291PA99


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


351 N.C. 627; 527 S.E.2d 921; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 349


February 16, 2000, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 5, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 from a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 133 N.C. App. 292, 515 S.E.2d 488 (1999), finding no error in a judgment entered by Ragan, J., on 25 February 1998 in Superior Court, Craven County. On 19 August 1999, this Court allowed the State's petition for discretionary review as to additional issues.



DISPOSITION: MODIFIED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the driving while impaired charge. The District Court, Craven County (North Carolina) denied defendant's motion to dismiss or to suppress, and defendant was found guilty. Defendant appealed the judgment of the North Carolina Court of Appeals, which found no error in defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: The court held that it was constitutionally permissible for an officer to stop a vehicle which had made a legal turn away from a posted driving while impaired checkpoint. The officer observed a "quick left turn" away from the checkpoint at the precise point where the driver of the vehicle would have first become aware of its presence. However, the officer did not stop defendant's vehicle once it turned away from the checkpoint. In fact, the court could not conclude that the officer "stopped" defendant's vehicle at any point. Defendant voluntarily parked in a residential driveway and remained hidden in the car until the officer approached the vehicle. Therefore, defendant was not "seized" by the police officer until at least that point. Also, based upon that series of incriminating circumstances, the officer observed sufficient activity to raise a reasonable and articulable suspicion of criminal activity. Therefore, the court found no error in defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Judgment modified and affirmed; it was constitutionally permissible for officer to make an investigatory stop of defendant's vehicle which had turned away, attempting to avoid a driving while impaired checkpoint. Based on the totality of the circumstances the officer had reasonable and articulable suspicion of criminal activity. Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Wallace


No. 241A97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


351 N.C. 481; 528 S.E.2d 326; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 350


November 16, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 5, 2000, Filed  [***1] 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 27, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 7911.
Writ of certiorari denied Wallace v. North Carolina, 531 U.S. 1018, 121 S. Ct. 581, 148 L. Ed. 2d 498, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 7911 (2000)
Writ denied by State v. Wallace, 360 N.C. 76, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 1121 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Summary judgment granted by, Summary judgment denied by Wallace v. Polk, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 36679 (W.D.N.C., May 5, 2008)
Certificate of appealability denied Wallace v. Polk, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 79979 (W.D.N.C., Aug. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing nine sentences of death entered by Johnston, J., on 29 January 1997 in Superior Court, Mecklenburg County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of nine counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 9 March 1999.
State v. Wallace, 351 N.C. 646, 543 S.E.2d 882, 2000 N.C. LEXIS 369 (2000)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing nine sentences of death entered by the Superior Court, Mecklenburg County (North Carolina). Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death on each of nine counts of first-degree murder. He had confessed to the murders. The supreme court found that the short-form indictments used for the murder charges and to charge other crimes were constitutional; U.S. Const. amend. XIV did not require an indictment to list all elements or facts which might increase the maximum punishment for a crime. The trial court acted properly in denying a change of venue and in denying defendant's motion to suppress his confession; the confession was not the result of a delay in taking defendant before a magistrate. Defendant was not prejudiced by references made during cross-examination of defense experts to additional murders to which defendant had confessed. The pattern instructions given on deliberation adequately covered the substance of defendant's requested instructions. There was no error in instructions given during the sentencing proceeding on mitigating and aggravating circumstances, nor did the prosecution's sentencing phase closing argument require a mistrial. The death sentences were not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and death sentences were upheld. The indictments were proper; there was no error in refusing to change venue or suppress defendant's confession; instructions during the guilt and sentencing phases were proper; death sentences were supported by aggravating circumstances.

State v. Roseboro


No. 156A94-2


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


351 N.C. 536; 528 S.E.2d 1; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 352


September 15, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 5, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 27, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 7916.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Patti, J., on 29 August 1997 in Superior Court, Gaston County, upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered in Superior Court, Gaston County (North Carolina), upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: In a capital case, defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder; he was also convicted of first-degree burglary, first-degree rape, felonious larceny, and possession of stolen property. At defendant's second capital sentencing proceeding, the jury recommended the death sentence. Defendant failed to follow mandatory procedures set forth in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1214(h) to preserve his exception to the ruling on his challenge for cause during jury selection. Defendant also contended that his constitutional rights to a fair and impartial jury and a fair sentencing hearing were denied by failing to excuse prospective jurors who were tainted by remarks of pro-death penalty prospective jurors. The court disagreed. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a peremptory instruction on mitigating circumstances. The case was not substantially similar to any case in which a court found the death penalty disproportionate. The sentence of death was left undisturbed.


OUTCOME: The sentence of death was left undisturbed. Defendant's death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate. Defendant received a fair capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error.

Bailey v. State


No. 53PA96-2


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


351 N.C. 440; 526 S.E.2d 657; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 230


December 14, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 7, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of an order entered by Thompson, J., on 23 April 1999 in Superior Court, Wake County. WAKE COUNTY NO. 92CVS10221. WAKE COUNTY NO. 94CVS06904. WAKE COUNTY NO. 95CVS04346. WAKE COUNTY NO. 95CVS06625. WAKE COUNTY NO. 95CVS08230. WAKE COUNTY NO. 98CVS00738.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Discretionary review of the order of the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), which decreed that the effective date of the first payment installment was July 1, 1998, with interest accruing to the benefit of plaintiffs from that date.


OVERVIEW: The trial court decreed that the effective date of the transfer of the first payment in a settlement fund was July 1, 1998, with interest accruing to the benefit of plaintiffs from that date. The State appealed, and the parties filed a joint petition for discretionary review. The court held that the consent order, the pertinent legislation, and the court order approving the settlement revealed that the effective date of the first installment was July 1, 1998. The consent order provided that the settlement became effective upon the enactment of legislation and court approval. The legislative act establishing the reserve fund provided that its effective date was July 1, 1998. The court order allocated distribution of the funds as of the effective date prescribed in the legislative act. Defendants were obligated to pay the principal as of that date and the interest began accruing on that date.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed; the consent order, the pertinent legislation, and the court order approving the settlement revealed that the effective date of the first installment was July 1, 1998, and the trial court properly provided that interest began accruing on that date.

State v. Gell


No. 469A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


351 N.C. 192; 524 S.E.2d 332; 2000 N.C. LEXIS 1


October 13, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 4, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5783.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Meyer, J., on 2 March 1998 in Superior Court, Bertie County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 22 March 1999.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right from Superior Court, Bertie County (North Carolina) his convictions for first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, robbery with a firearm, and conspiracy to commit robbery with a firearm, and his sentence of death for the first-degree murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: At a trial by jury, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit murder, robbery with a firearm, and conspiracy to commit robbery with a firearm. In a separate proceeding, he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed as of right contending that the trial court erred in how it handled the jury voir dire and jury instructions; in how it handled prior statements of the co-conspirators; by failing to intervene when the prosecutor made in inappropriate comments during closing arguments; in allowing evidence of crimes committed after the murder in the mitigation phase of sentencing; and various other arguments. Although the court did find prosecutor's comments were improper and some evidence was improperly admitted during sentencing, the court found the trial and sentencing proceeding was free of prejudicial error. The court also concluded the death sentence was not disproportionate. Therefore, the court upheld the convictions and the death sentence.

OUTCOME: No error found.

State v. Stroessenreuther


No. COA16-151


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


793 S.E.2d 734; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 1240


August 10, 2016, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
December 6, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] New Hanover County, No. 15 CRS 50624.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a trial court properly imposed lifetime satellite-based monitoring upon defendant pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-208.40A. HOLDINGS: [1]-North Carolina's satellite-based monitoring laws were not facially unconstitutional because case law held that trial courts were to consider a challenge to satellite-based monitoring under U.S. Const. amend. IV when a defendant raised it; [2]-Defendant's as-applied challenge was meritorious because the trial court was required to consider the reasonableness of the satellite-based monitoring when defendant challenged that monitoring under U.S. Const. amend. IV. However, the trial court did not conduct that inquiry; [3]-The imposition of satellite-based monitoring had to be vacated, and the case remanded for the trial court to conduct the necessary reasonableness inquiry described in the case law.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated, and case remanded for further proceedings.

Settlers Edge Holding Co., LLC v. RES-NC Settlers Edge, LLC


No. COA15-1055


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


793 S.E.2d 722; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 1235



December 6, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Settlers Edge Holding Co., LLC v. RES-NC Settlers Edge, LLC, 797 S.E.2d 15, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 178 (N.C., Mar. 16, 2017)
Review dismissed by, As moot Settlers Edge Holding Co., LLC v. RES-NC Settlers Edge, LLC, 797 S.E.2d 295, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 177 (N.C., Mar. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Yancey County, No. 10 CVS 279.
Settlers Edge Holding Co. v. RES-NC Settlers Edge, LLC, 238 N.C. App. 198, 768 S.E.2d 66, 2014 N.C. App. LEXIS 1291 (Dec. 16, 2014)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Barring plaintiff developer's affirmative defense of repudiation to a breach of contract counterclaim by defendant, an insolvent bank's receiver's assignee, erred because no formal 12 U.S.C.S. § 1821(e)(2) repudiation occurred, the assignee sought damages from the developer, and the receiver effectively repudiated; [2]-The assignee was not entitled to summary judgment because, while 12 U.S.C.S. § 1821(e)(3)(A) limited the developer's recoupment damages to compensatory damages, fact issues existed as to the sum the developer was entitled to; [3]-A clerk's order finding the developer not in default was not entitled to collateral estoppel effect because no material breach was clearly found, and, if a breach occurred, recovery was limited to recoupment; [4]-The developer was not entitled to summary judgment because the offset for the assignee's breach had to be considered.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

N.C. State Bar v. Sutton


No. COA15-1198


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


791 S.E.2d 881; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 1069


April 25, 2016, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 18, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by N.C. State Bar v. Sutton, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 223 (N.C., Mar. 16, 2017)
Motion denied by NC State Bar v. Sutton, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 220 (N.C., Mar. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Disciplinary Hearing Commission of the North Carolina State Bar, No. 13 DHC 11.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The attorney provided no basis for his assertion that the State Bar's actions usurped the role the judiciary in regulating attorney misconduct; [2]-The attorney's claim that the Rules of Professional Conduct were unconstitutional because they allowed him to be punished for protected speech lacked merit, as the First Amendment did not immunize an attorney from discipline simply because the attorney employed "speech" in committing the violations; [3]-The attorney was properly suspended from practice of law for five years after he violated various rules of professional conduct by interjecting questions and commentary into a deposition and coaching the deponent, leaving a deposition without filing a motion to terminate it, and sending a demand letter to an individual he knew was represented by counsel.


OUTCOME: Order of discipline affirmed.

OUTCOME: No error found.

OUTCOME: Order reversed.

State v. Cobb

COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


789 S.E.2d 532; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 823

August 2, 2016, Filed

DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress because he voluntarily consented to the search of his room , where he was not in custody at the time he gave consent, as the officers' mere presence at his home did not equate to constant police supervision. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Herron v. N.C. Bd. of Examiners for Eng'rs & Surveyors


No. COA15-1382


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


790 S.E.2d 321; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 704


May 26, 2016, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
July 5, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Buncombe County, No. 13 CVS 4551.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a trial court properly reversed an order by the North Carolina Board of Examiners for Engineers and Surveyors that revoked a land surveyor's license. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred by holding that the land surveyor's due process rights were violated by the procedure which the Board utilized because, although the Board technically approved a settlement conference committee's recommendation, it did not prejudge the adjudicative facts of the case and made its decision without learning that the committee recommended revocation of the land surveyor's license and without any exposure to the evidence or investigation that had led to this recommendation. Furthermore, there was no showing of bias in the Board's decision.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, and case remanded for further proceedings.

Anderson v. N.C. State Bd. of Elections


No. COA14-1369


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


788 S.E.2d 179; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 663


August 12, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
June 21, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Wake County, No. 14 CVS 12648.
Anderson v. N.C. State Bd. of Elections, 367 N.C. 802, 764 S.E.2d 468, 2014 N.C. LEXIS 882 (2014)



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Respondent North Carolina State Board of Elections' (Board) appeal of an order to adopt an early voting plan was moot because the election was held, and petitioners voters received requested relief; [2]-The capable of repetition yet evading review mootness exception did not let the Board's jurisdictional claim under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 163-22(l) (2015) be considered because the same voters were unlikely to be subject to the same action, as the "same action" was not the Board's defense of a future plan but if future voters would claim a plan violated the constitutional rights of voters aged 18 to 25, and the Board was not the same "complaining party"; [2]-The public interest exception to mootness did not apply because the Board did not show why its jurisdictional claim deserved prompt resolution or how the judicial review the voters obtained implicated a great public interest.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.

Glenn v. Johnson


No. COA15-523


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


787 S.E.2d 65; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 611


October 22, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
June 7, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Orange County, No. 13 CVS 2082.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in entering summary judgment in favor of a church and its chairmen because a church member failed to establish a prima facie case of negligence inflection of emotional distress; [2]-The member never identified the chairmen's negligent conduct, and the only conceivable duty they owed to the member was to act in accordance with the bylaws of the church, but any conduct by the chairmen in contravention to the bylaws was intentional, rather than negligent; [3]-The trial court did not err in entering summary judgment in favor of the church and chairmen on the member's intentional infliction of emotional distress claim because the member failed to allege or present evidence that their conduct rose to the level of extreme and outrageous; [4]-The conduct alleged to be extreme and outrageous included requesting that the member, as treasurer, write checks.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed.

Gen. Stat. § 115C-325.4(a)(1), (4), (9), and (10) (2014), because supporting evidence could be considered, and he got an N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C-325.6(b) (2014) notice.

In re S.Z.H.


No. COA15-1270


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA

May 3, 2016, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Randolph County, No. 14 JT 75.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Clear evidence did not support the finding that the father failed to maintain communications with the child during the relevant time; [2]-The evidence tended to show that the father attempted to communicate with the child but the mother stopped allowing him to contact her; [3]-Certain findings addressed factual grounds that could support a conclusion of abandonment and some of them addressed events outside the relevant six-month period, and other findings, including that there had been no cards or gifts from the father to the child, and that the father failed to provide support, did not demonstrate that he had a willful determination to forego all parental duties and relinquish all parental claims to the child; [4]-The trial court erred in concluding that the father had willfully abandoned the child for purposes of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7B-1111(a)(7).


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

State v. Bedient


No. COA15-1011


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


786 S.E.2d 319; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 506


February 22, 2016, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
May 3, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Jackson County, No. 13 CRS 50269.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The facts that defendant was engaging in nervous behavior and she had associated with a known drug dealer were insufficient to support the trial court's conclusion that the officer had reasonable suspicion to prolong defendant's detention after the purpose of the traffic stop had concluded; [2]-Because the officer continued to possess defendant's driver's license up until the moment he received her consent to search her car and only returned the license upon commencing the search, the stop was unlawfully extended and violated defendant's Fourth Amendment right and therefore defendant's consent was not voluntary.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

State v. Singletary


No. COA15-1125


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


786 S.E.2d 712; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 500


March 31, 2016, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
May 3, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Guilford County, No. 13 CRS 92516-17, 92519-20.



DISPOSITION: NO PREJUDICIAL ERROR AT TRIAL; JUDGMENT VACATED; REMANDED FOR NEW SENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in not allowing defendant to further inquire into the amount of an expert's compensation during cross-examination, however, the error was harmless, as the jury heard testimony as to the source of the expert's compensation and there was overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt; [2]-The trial court did not err in declining to give a requested pattern jury instruction on testimony of an interested witness, as it provided the requested instruction on interest or bias "in substance" through the use of an alternate instruction; [3]-Former N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-27.4A(c) (now O.C.G.A. § 14-27.28) violated defendant's rights under the Sixth Amendment by permitting the court to increase the penalty beyond a prescribed statutory maximum without submitting the issue to a jury for proof beyond a reasonable doubt, and thus, resentencing was necessary.


OUTCOME: No prejudicial error at trial. Judgment vacated and remanded for new sentencing hearing.

Motion granted by State v. James, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 445 (N.C., June 14, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Mecklenburg County, No. 06 CRS 222499.
State v. James, 216 N.C. App. 417, 716 S.E.2d 876, 2011 N.C. App. LEXIS 2266 (Oct. 18, 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1340.19A et seq., did not violate the prohibitions on ex post facto laws in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 or N.C. Const. art. I, § 16, as it did not imposed a different or greater punishment than was permitted when the crime was committed, but provided sentencing guidelines requiring a court to consider mitigating circumstances before imposing a sentence of life without paroles for a juvenile; [2]-The appellate court held that it was not inappropriate or unconstitutional for the sentencing analysis in § 15A-1340.19A et seq. to begin with a sentence of life without parole and require the sentencing court to consider mitigating factors to determine whether a juvenile offender should be sentenced to life with or without parole; [3]-The trial court's findings were insufficient since they did not demonstrate the absence of presence of mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, reversed and remanded in part.

PURSUANT TO RULE 32(b), NORTH CAROLINA RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE TWENTY-ONE DAY REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Bonetsky, 785 S.E.2d 323, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 394 (N.C., May 13, 2016)

Review denied by, Stay denied by State v. Bonetsky, 786 S.E.2d 917, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 510 (N.C., June 9, 2016)

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case in which defendant appealed his conviction of possession of a firearm by a felon, the appellate court concluded that the State established that defendant's "as applied" challenge to N.C. Gen. Stat § 14-415.1 under N.C. Const. art. I, § 30, failed as a matter of law; [2]-The fact that defendant's right to possess a firearm at his home may have been restored under Texas law did not mean that right was restored under North Carolina law; [3]-The trial court did not err by finding there was no indication that defendant had taken any affirmative action to comply with the statute; [4]-The appellate court could not say defendant had affirmatively demonstrated that he was not among the class of citizens who pose a threat to public peace and safety and that there was no rational basis under which § 14-415.1 could apply to him.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed.
