State v. Miller


No. COA15-636


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


783 S.E.2d 512; 2016 N.C. App. LEXIS 295


November 18, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
March 15, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by State v. Miller, 368 N.C. 821, 783 S.E.2d 502, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 298 (Mar. 31, 2016)
Review granted by, Stay granted by, Appeal dismissed by State v. Miller, 368 N.C. 917, 787 S.E.2d 21, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 456 (June 9, 2016)
Reversed by State v. Miller, 2017 N.C. LEXIS 395 (N.C., June 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Watauga County, No. 14 CRS 50091.



DISPOSITION: VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-N.C. Gen. Stat. § 90-95(d1)(1)(c) (2013), making possession of a product containing pseudoephedrine by a person previously convicted of possessing methamphetamine a felony, was a strict liability crime because the general assembly intentionally included no intent element, as other subdivisions of the statute included such an element; [2]-Defendant's conviction under the statute violated due process because he had no notice that he was subject to criminal penalties for an act legal for most people, before the subsection was enacted, it was legal for him to buy pseudoephedrine products, there were no circumstances which might move one to inquire as to a significant change in the law's requirements, and no proof beyond a reasonable doubt that he was aware that his possession of a pseudoephedrine product was illegal.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated.

OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Booth v. State


No. COA15-640


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


781 S.E.2d 88; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 1042


November 19, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
December 15, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Wake County, No. 12 CV 180.
Booth v. State, 227 N.C. App. 484, 742 S.E.2d 637, 2013 N.C. App. LEXIS 606 (2013)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case concerning firearm rights, a convicted felon's right to seek redress of grievances did not entitle him to compel a ruling by the courts on each and every claim he set forth, particularly when a court's determination on one issue rendered another issue moot or unnecessary; [2]-A prior decision determined that the current version of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-415.1 did not apply to the convicted felon, as he had his firearm rights restored; therefore, no real and existing controversy remained; [3]-The declaratory relief sought had been received, and the constitutional question was not addressed on appeal.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. McGee


No. COA15-722


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


780 S.E.2d 916; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 1044


November 19, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
December 15, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Forsyth County, No. 07 CRS 22500, 37901, 53099, 53100-01, 62549; 08 CR 053753-54 [**1] , 053697.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's argument that the trial court failed to comply with N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 15A-1023(b) or 15A-1024 was barred by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1027 where his motion for appropriate relief (MAR) was filed more than seven years after the 14-day appeal period allowed by N.C. R. App. P. 4(a) (2008), and as a result, the MAR was a collateral attack; [2]-The court's holding did not diminish a trial court's duty, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 15A-1023 and 15A-1024, to grant a continuance until the next session of court, following the rejection by the trial court of a guilty plea or the imposition of a sentence other than provided for in a plea arrangement; [3]-The holding did not diminish a defendant's ability to pursue appellate review, in open court or during the appeal period, of alleged violations of the procedural requirements found in article 58 of chapter 15A.


OUTCOME: Motion to dismiss appeal granted.

State v. Biddix

DISPOSITION: DENIED and DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's appeal following a guilty plea, asserting his plea was not the product of an informed choice when the terms of his plea agreement were contradictory, had to be dismissed because he had no statutory right to appeal this issue, under N.C. App. P. 2 to suspend the requirements of N.C. R. App. P. 21 (2015), as he showed no "exceptional circumstances," as he received a sentence consistent with his guilty plea, acknowledgement of an aggravating factor, and understanding the sentence rested within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: Petition denied, appeal dismissed.

State v. Fryou


No. COA14-1168


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


780 S.E.2d 152; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 952


April 8, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
November 17, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Fryou, 781 S.E.2d 479, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 65 (N.C., Jan. 28, 2016)
Review denied by State v. Fryou, 781 S.E.2d 483, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 62 (N.C., Jan. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Avery County, No. 12CRS050717.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-208.18(a) (2011), whether defendant had been convicted of a crime involving a victim under 16 was a jury question because this was a fact question; [2]-Sufficient evidence showed defendant's "knowing" violation because the State did not have to show minors were present when he was there, and the evidence showed he knew a child care facility was run on the premises; [3]-He had no standing to claim statutory overbreadth because his claims unrelated to expression did not qualify him for expanded First Amendment standing, and he raised no other constitutional right; [4]-His vagueness claim based on the premises' use as a church and a child care facility failed because N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-208.18(a)(2) (2011) barred his presence at any premises containing a facility used to supervise minors, even if it was not operating when he was there.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

R. App. P. 21 and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1444, the appellate court was unable to issue a writ of certiorari.

State v. Mastor

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Pursuant to N.C. Gen. City of Asheville v. State


No. COA14-1255

777 S.E.2d 92; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 823


June 3, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
October 6, 2015, Filed

PURSUANT TO RULE 32(b), NORTH CAROLINA RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE TWENTY-ONE DAY REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 778 S.E.2d 439, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1190 (2015)
Review granted by, Stay granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 476, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 36 (2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 473, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 39 (2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 474, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 43 (2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 795, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 45 (2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 477, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 46 (2016)
Motion denied by City of Asheville v. State, 368 N.C. 686, 781 S.E.2d 474, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 47 (2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 781 S.E.2d 803, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 156 (N.C., 2016)
Motion granted by City of Asheville v. State, 784 S.E.2d 170, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 293 (N.C., 2016)
Reversed by City of Asheville v. State, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 1133 (N.C., Dec. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Wake County, No. 13-CVS-6691.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiff city had standing to contest the constitutionality of the Water/Sewer Act (Act), N.C. Gen. Stat. § 162A-85.1 et seq., making it to cede control of its water system to another entity because cities had such standing, and it had accepted no benefit of the Act; [2]-The Act did not violate N.C. Const. art. II, § 24 because it did not regulate health or sanitation or relate to non-navigable streams, so it was not a "local" law; [3]-It did not violate N.C. Const. art. I, § 19 because, if it irrationally singled out the city, it was only a "local" law, and it did not violate the bar against such laws; [4]-It did not violate N.C. Const. art. I, §§ 19 and 35 by exceeding the state's authority to take property or taking the city's property without compensation because a legislature could assign a city's proprietary endeavor to another entity without consent or compensation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.

Credit Union Auto Buying Serv. v. Burkshire Props. Grp. Corp.


No. COA15-187


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


243 N.C. App. 12; 776 S.E.2d 737; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 774


August 26, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
September 15, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forsyth County, No. 14 CVS 3592.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The denial of appellant New York company's motion to dismiss was immediately reviewable, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-277, because the motion alleged a lack of personal jurisdiction; [2]-The motion was properly denied because a North Carolina court was authorized to exercise quasi in rem jurisdiction, under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 1-75.8 (2013), as appellee corporation's claim concerned a security interest in vehicles it bought and certificates of title to the vehicles, the vehicles were located in North Carolina and their ownership was central to the controversy, and the company was not unaware that North Carolina was the vehicles' destination.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

199 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perry


No. COA14-1328


COURT OF APPEALS OF NORTH CAROLINA


243 N.C. App. 156; 776 S.E.2d 528; 2015 N.C. App. LEXIS 769


June 1, 2015, Heard in the Court of Appeals 
September 15, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Appeal dismissed by State v. Perry, 368 N.C. 683, 781 S.E.2d 622, 2016 N.C. LEXIS 123 (N.C., Jan. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wake County, Nos. 12 CRS 227771, 13 CRS 3178.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-It was no error not to suppress records of the location of defendant's cell phone because these were historical stored third-party records properly disclosed under a court order, pursuant to 18 U.S.C.S. § 2703(d), retrieval of this information was not a "search" requiring a warrant under the Fourth Amendment or N.C. Const. art. I, § 20, as no physical trespass occurred, he showed no GPS or "real-time" tracking, he voluntarily conveyed the information to his provider, so he showed no reasonable expectation of privacy, and the good-faith exception to the warrant requirement applied, as an officer relied on procedures in the Stored Communications Act, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2703(d), to obtain the information; [2]-Defendant was not entitled to disclosure of sealed documents because they contained no information favorable and material to his guilt or punishment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
